```
A bit of knowledge of Biblical Hebrew makes this is a beautiful, stinging 
insult, Mr Brazee; the trigrammatic root often translated as 'righteous' 
is tsadi-dalet-kaph.

The masculine plural is often transliterated as 'Tzadikim', folks who are 
accorded a great reverence.  See http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tzadik for a 
list beginning with the Book of Genisis' Joseph.

DD
```

```
Alistair Maclean wrote:
> On Mar 1, 1:49 pm, "HeyBub" <hey...@NOSPAMgmail.com> wrote:
>> Howard Brazee wrote:
…[20 more quoted lines elided]…
> How can one be a righteous atheist?

I manage it pretty well... :-)

Being righteous has nothing to do with religious belief, unless you are 
indctrinated into a religion at an early age. Then you tend to believe it is 
your religious belief that makes you righteous. In fact it isn't. It is 
plain common sense that if we treat each other well the world becomes a 
better place. The fact that these simple truths were recognised by ancient 
teachers and moulded into all of the world's great religions does NOT mean 
that these religions INVENTED them. Neither does it mean that the ONLY path 
to enlightenment and understanding is through religion.

I have had people say to me: "How can you have morals or ethics unless you 
have a religious belief?" even despite them knowing that I do in fact apply 
these things in my everyday life.

I used to be hurt by it; now I just smile.

I guess I have grown...

Pete
```

- **Message-ID:** `<9rc278FcgbU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
Pete Dashwood wrote:
> About 3 years ago I wrote an article about the relevance of COBOL.
>
…[50 more quoted lines elided]…
> Pete.

This article has now taken almost 100 hits, many times my expectations.

It has been pointed out to me that if Javascript is disabled in the Browser, 
Heisenberg just waits indefinitely, the seconds don't clock down, but 
neither do they appear, so the sentence "... in 25 seconds" reads as "in 
seconds" and this still makes sense. Several people were amused by this, 
although Browsing the Web with Javascript disabled, to me, is as timid as 
driving a senior mobility cart instead of a car, because speed kills.

(I confess a bias; I took time to write the javascript...:-))

Thanks to all.

The best comment that has been made to date was:

"It is relevant to anyone who is being paid to code in it." :-)

Pete.
```

## Thread: IF JESUS WAS GOD !!!!!!!!!!!!!!! — 5 msgs

### IF JESUS WAS GOD !!!!!!!!!!!!!!!

- **From:** BV BV <bv4bv4bv4@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2012-03-04T08:47:10-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<3aaaff08-918c-4e9f-8e00-9707b6a4b66e@i2g2000vbv.googlegroups.com>`

```
IF JESUS WAS GOD

If Jesus was GOD, then why in Mark 12:29 Jesus said "Here, O Israel:
The Lord our God is one Lord." The words "our God" indicate that Jesus
had a higher God over him, a stronger God than him. Jesus didn't say
"Your God". He said "our God" which includes Jesus as the creation of
GOD.
If Jesus was GOD, then why in John 20:17 Jesus said I ascend to my God
and your God? This tells us that we and Jesus have a common GOD.
If Jesus was GOD, then why in John 8:28 Jesus said "I do nothing of
myself"? Can't GOD do anything he wills?

If Jesus was GOD, then why in John 14:28 Jesus said "My Father (GOD)
is greater than I"?If Jesus was GOD, then why in Luke 23:46 Jesus said
"Father (GOD), into thy hands I commend my spirit"?
If Jesus was GOD, then why in Matthew 19:16 Jesus said "Why call me
good, there is none good but One, that is GOD"?

If Jesus was GOD, then why in Matthew 26:39 Jesus begged his GOD to
have mercy on him and to pass the cup to death (kill Jesus in another
words) before Jesus goes through the pain of
crucifixion? Also see: Jesus's crucifixion in Islam

If Jesus was GOD, then why in John 18:38 he didn't reply when he was
asked about the truth?

If Jesus was GOD, then why in Matthew 24:36 Jesus told his followers
that no one (including Jesus) knows when the judgment day will come,
only GOD knows?
If Jesus was GOD, then why in Isiah 11:2-3 GOD had put the spirit of
fearing GOD in Jesus?

If Jesus was GOD, then why in John 5:31 Jesus told his followers that
if he (Jesus) bears witness of himself, then his record is not true?

If Jesus was GOD, then why in John 5:30 Jesus told his followers that
he can't do a single thing of his own initiative?

If Jesus was GOD, then why in John 5:36-38 Jesus said that GOD had
assigned him (Jesus) work and GOD is a witness on Jesus?

If Jesus was GOD, then why in John 5:32 Jesus told his followers that
they have never seen GOD at anytime nor ever heard his voice?

If Jesus was GOD, then why did he pray to his GOD in Luke 5:16?

If Jesus was GOD, then why in Matthew 26:39 Jesus fell on his face and
prayed to his GOD?

The "God" Title:
How come Christians take the "God" (theos in Greek) title literally
with Jesus in Isiah 9:6 and they don't take it literally for the rest
of the prophets and people who were called Gods ?
The Prophets who were called "God" in the Bible are as follows:
Prophet Moses in Exodus 7:1
The Devil in Corinthians 4:4 (the word for God in this verse is theos
in Greek, the same used for Jesus that was translated as "God")
Multiple Prophets in Psalms 82:6
King David in Psalm 45:3
Note: The only unique title given to GOD in the Bible that was not
given to others at all are Jehova, GOD, and GOD LORD. "God", "Most
Mighty" and "Almighty One" are titles that were given to Jesus, other
Prophets and to Satan himself in the Bible.

Very important note: Did you know that in the languages of Arabic and
Hebrew the father of the house can be called the God of the house?
Jesus was the God (father or leader) of his people and their father
according to Isiah 9:6. Jesus being the leader and the king, it is
normal for him to be called the father of his people (Father in Isiah
9:6), and because he is their father he automatically becomes their
God. My father is my God in Arabic and Hebrew.

The "Son" Title:
How come Christians take the "God's Son" title literally with Jesus
and they don't take it literally for the rest of the prophets and
people who were called the Sons of God?
In John 3:16 Jesus was called God's only Begotten Son.
In Exodus 4:22 "Thus saith Jehova, Isreal is my son, even my
firstborn." Isreal was called God's First Son.
In Jeremiah 31:9 "I am a father to Isreal, and Ephraim is my
firstborn." Ephraim is God's First Son and First Born.In Psalm 2:7
"... Jehova had said onto me (David), thou art my Son; this day have I
begotten thee." David was called God's Begotten Son.

Were Jesus's Miracle's Unique?
If Jesus is believed to be GOD because he could do miracles, he could
heal leprosy, he could cause blind men to see, or raise the dead, then
what about the others who performed the same miracles?

Elisha and Elijah fed a hundred people with twenty barley loaves and a
few ears of corn (2 Kings 4:44).

[Elisha told Naaman, who was a leper, to wash in the river Jordan (2
Kings 5:14) and he was healed. Elisha caused a blind man to see in (2
Kings 6:17,20).

Elijah and Elisha raised the dead in (1 Kings 17:22, and 2 Kings
4:34). Even Elisha's dead bones restored a dead body in (2 Kings
13:21).
Indeed Jesus had prophesied that people will worship him uselessly and
will believe in doctrines not made by GOD but by men "But in vain they
do worship me, teaching for doctrines the commandments of men.
(Matthew 15:9)"

In Matthew 15:9 above, we see Jesus warning that Trinity (the bogus
lie) will dominate, and people will take Jesus as GOD and worship him,
which is a total sin according to what Jesus said !!
Allah Almighty (GOD) in the Noble Quran (The Muslims' Holy Scripture)
states in Verse 5:72 "They do blaspheme who say: 'God is Christ the
son of Mary.' But said Christ: 'O Children of Isreal ! worship God, my
Lord and your Lord.' "

Also in Noble Verse 5:73 "They do blaspheme who say God is one of
three in a Trinity: for there is no god except One God. If they desist
not from their word (of blasphemy), verily a grievous penalty will
befall the blasphemers among them."
And also in Noble Verse 4:171 "O People of the Book! Commit no
excesses in your religion: Nor say of God aught but the truth. Christ
Jesus the son of Mary was (no more than) an apostle of God, ..."

The Point that I am trying to prove:

Muslims believe that Prophet Jesus peace be upon him is a messenger
from God. He was sent from God Almighty to deliver God's words to his
people. Jesus was never God, nor ever claimed to be God. Jesus was a
humble wonderful human being just like the rest of the Prophets and
Messengers of God. Muslims also believe that Jesus was never
crucified, nor ever died on the cross, nor ever wanted to die on the
cross, nor ever was sent to earth to die on the cross .
```

```
On Mar 6, 6:41 am, Alistair Maclean <alistair.j.l.macl...@gmail.com>
wrote:
> On Mar 4, 4:47 pm, BV BV <bv4bv4...@gmail.com> wrote:
>
> > IF JESUS WAS GOD

It may be interestring to know what people mean by the term 'god'.

Alexander was a God. Hirohito was a God until the allies made him stop
being one. Haile Selassie is still is a God to the Rastafarians. The
Pharaohs were God-Kings, the Caesars were Gods after they died. There
were many other Gods that, most likely, were actual people with their
abilities and exploits exaggerated, rather than being wholly
fictional.

I see no reason to think that Jehovah was anything other than a local
[war]lord, or perhaps a dynasty of them. The fables and legends of the
earlier books can be dismissed as mere puffery. In the Canaanite
legends their main God was El and he is said to have had many
children, among them was a Jehovah and several Bael (or Baal), eg Bael
Zebub. The bible has Jehovah as 'one of the Elohim': the family or
house of El.

So the term 'God' means a man who has ultimate power in the form of
being a king, emperor or warlord, but who has also been recorded with
a fair amount of exaggeration and puffery.
```

## Thread: Object Oriented Fujitsu Cobol example — 3 msgs

_Topics: [`Compilers and vendors`](topics.md#compilers) · [`Object-oriented COBOL`](topics.md#oo)_

### Object Oriented Fujitsu Cobol example

- **From:** Zalek Bloom <zalekbloom@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2012-03-05T16:38:49-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<ef2bf981-d29f-464d-9172-7b69fab9acee@q12g2000vbt.googlegroups.com>`

```
I am looking for any example of Object Oriented Fujitsu Cobol source.

Is it worth to convert regular batch Fujitsu Cobol to OO?

Thanks,

Zalek
```

#### ↳ Re: Object Oriented Fujitsu Cobol example

- **From:** Richard <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-03-05T17:37:37-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<c23a7a0a-3077-4c28-bcb1-ad3109deb9ad@jx1g2000pbb.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<ef2bf981-d29f-464d-9172-7b69fab9acee@q12g2000vbt.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Mar 6, 1:38 pm, Zalek Bloom <zalekbl...@gmail.com> wrote:

> I am looking for any example of Object Oriented Fujitsu Cobol source.

Here's one that I prepared earlier.


http://groups.google.com/group/comp.lang.cobol/browse_frm/thread/41f28746f0fe0366/809a400124d02abe?lnk=gst&q=rawprint#809a400124d02abe


> Is it worth to convert regular batch Fujitsu Cobol to OO?

One real advantage of OO is that it is possible to have multiple
instances of an object, each encapsulated so that they can be operated
on in the manner they require.

Batch programs usually only require a single instance of each item and
process using serial reuse. ie they usually only require a single
record area per file and reuse that area for each record in the file.
```

#### ↳ Re: Object Oriented Fujitsu Cobol example

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-03-06T15:53:28+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,alt.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9rlchbFaapU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<ef2bf981-d29f-464d-9172-7b69fab9acee@q12g2000vbt.googlegroups.com>`

```
Zalek Bloom wrote:
> I am looking for any example of Object Oriented Fujitsu Cobol source.

Please take a look at: http://primacomputing.co.nz/cobol21/

In particular... The link to the COBDATA Structure analyser tool.

"This is an example of standard COBOL  running on .NET. The underlying 
engine was written by Robert Wagner as standard procedural COBOL. See how it 
is easily converted to OO COBOL and wrapped as a COM component. Finally, a 
presentation layer is added in C# and the whole application becomes a .NET 
assembly.

Follow the link for full details and download of the tool itself, the COBOL 
sources (both standard and OO), and the C# source. "

It is a free tool which several hundred people have found useful, but, 
perhaps more importantly for you, it shows the changes needed to convert 
standard COBOL into OO COBOL. The original COBOL code is provided and the OO 
code is provided with the changes flagged in it.

>
> Is it worth to convert regular batch Fujitsu Cobol to OO?
>
I agree with Richard's assessment on this.

Generally, there is not much benefit in converting batch processes to OO 
COBOL.

HOWEVER, if there is functionality within that batch process which could be 
used elsewhere, then it certainly does no harm to extract that functionality 
(CALLed module, PERFORMED subroutine, even sections of inline code) and wrap 
it into an OO Component.

This means it can be easily reused in desktop or web based applications and 
it can still run in a batch process. (The batch process invokes the object 
methods just like any other desktop application.)

I would not advise taking a whole batch process and making it OO. Use OO 
COBOL to refactor the functions and processes that you don't want to lose in 
the future, and which you would like to have in any future environment you 
may set up.

Please also have a read of: 
http://primacomputing.co.nz/COBOL21/COBOLRelevance.aspx


Pete.
```

<a id="t-383e98b712"></a>
## Thread: Pushing SQL in COBOL with Oracle — 2 msgs

_Topics: [`Databases and SQL`](topics.md#databases)_

### Pushing SQL in COBOL with Oracle

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-03-08T15:13:18+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9rqiu0F2knU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
Sometimes the fact that Embedded SQL can't support DDL for RDBMS can be a 
problem.

If you want to create dynamic tables from COBOL you can't because there is 
no support for CREATE TABLE, for example.

When faced with this problem some years back I got round it by painstakingly 
analysing the Data Access Objects (DAO) and ActiveX Data
Objects (ADO) Object Models and wrking out how to implement them in COBOL. 
It was laborious  but I got what I needed. These days I could do it much 
more easily because I have learned more... :-)

As a result of this exercise, I have some OO COBOL components that implement 
DAO to create tables dynamically.

I'm currently working to implement support for Oracle DB into the Migration 
Toolset. As the Toolset already supports Access, Access 2007, PostgreSQL, 
MySQL, SQL Lite,  and SQL Server, I expected this to be fairly routine...

But Oracle is "something else..." :-)

I won't go into a rant here about what I really dislike in Oracle or why I 
would never use it personally, but I'm wondering if anyone has ever tried 
accessing Oracle through DAO?

I have it working and I eventually managed to get the right connection 
strings worked out, but there is ONE major problem. If I ask it how many 
tables it has, it lies. I invoke the get COUNT property on the TABDEFS 
collection and it tells me I have 5120 tables on a database instance that 
actually has about 40... As this number is used subsequently to limit 
iterative processing it isn't very long before the component throws an 
addressing exception because a COBOL table which stores table names has 
overflowed.

I realize this is kind of Twilight Zone for most COBOL guys, but if anyone 
is using Oracle and has an idea how I can obtain the number of tables 
attached to a given UserID (WITHOUT actually enumerating them; there has to 
be a property somewhere that is accessible in SQL...) please throw me a 
bone... :-)

I can probably get round it if I use .Net stuff (OLEDB provider), but I 
don't want to have to rewrite a COBOL component that is working fine in 
every other respect and with every other RDBMS, (especially as it is a DDL 
generator and does some complex processing.)

Pete.
```

#### ↳ Re: Pushing SQL in COBOL with Oracle

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-03-08T15:37:34+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9rqkbgFbddU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<9rqiu0F2knU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
Pete Dashwood wrote:
<snip>

I solved it.

Changed the picture of the COBOL count field to be large binary... :-)

Pete.
```

```
Alistair Maclean wrote:
> On Mar 12, 6:12 am, BV BV <bv8bv8...@gmail.com> wrote:
>> GENOCIDE IN THE TWENTY-FIRST CENTURY IN SYRIA

Syria is indeed a tragedy.

We are witnessing people coming out of the dark ages of fear and ignorance 
and demanding a better deal. Normally this process would take place over 
several hundred years but because of modern communication technology and 
wider educational opportunities it is being compressed into a decade or so.

The message is becoming clear to tyrants everywhere. Ideas have power and 
simply will not be suppressed by ruthless regimes. The world is moving 
forward and the legacy of centuries of despotic rule in some places is over. 
The emerging Democracies will be shaky and unstable, for they are not used 
to governing themselves and it will take time for them to get the experience 
they need. People who have clung to a blind faith for centuries and been 
controlled by their religions and a series of ruthless rulers who enforced 
their will are not going to be able to cope with sudden freedom very well. 
But they will get the hang of it, and the realization is growing that it is 
better to live free in a disorganised State than to be enslaved in an 
organised one.

I see the current unrest as a legacy of the last century. By the end of this 
one the world should be a better place for most of its inhabitants.

Education and communication will see to the mental requirements and 
technology will see to the physical.

Sadly, because it is being "rushed", and because of the nature of modern 
weaponry, the price is terrible and tragic.

Pete.
```

```
requires to be extracted from source systems and cleansed using SAP
BusinessObjects Data Quality XI 4.0 toolset.
	Products
	Colorways
	Suppliers - Mills, Factories, Finished Goods suppliers and
attributes
	Materials - Fabric, Sundries, Packaging/Labeling materials and
attributes
	Sourcing Configuration - Supplier associations for Products,
Colorways, Materials
	Bills of Material
	Specifications
	Cost Sheets
	Measurement Libraries (Points of Measures, Measurement Templates,
Grading Templates, and associated Thumbnails)
	Construction Libraries (Construction details, Construction
Templates, and associated Thumbnails)
	Sizing Templates
	Colors (Color attributes, Thumbnails)
	Documents (File attachments)
	Image Pages (Fit Samples, Sketches, Photos, Fabric images, Other
Image files)

In order to accomplish the above, LS&CO requires a SAP BusinessObjects
Data Quality XI Specialist to perform the following job duties:
•	Recommend best practice solutions for Data migration and cleansing
using SAP BusinessObjects Data Quality Management toolset
•	Develop a SAP BusinessObjects Data Quality XI 4.0 based solution
that addresses profiling, parsing, standardization, cleansing,
matching for supplier, product and material data, both structured and
unstructured available in multiple file formats
•	Setup automatic validation logic for supplier, product and material
data using SAP BusinessObjects Data Quality XI 4.0
•	Develop data quality dashboards and reporting using SAP
BusinessObjects Data Quality XI 4.0 to measure, track and control
cleansing progress
•	Develop materials and train business cleansing team on how to use
SAP BusinessObjects Data Quality XI 4.0 for cleansing (step-by-step
instructions) for the various data objects in product, material and
supplier data domains



Skills and Experience
•	Expert level knowledge and hands on experience in ETL tools and
utilities
•	Expert level knowledge and hands on experience in using SAP
BusinessObjects Data Quality XI 4.0 for Data Migration and Cleansing
in large projects
•	Worked as a Data Migration and Cleansing Consultant in at least 3
large projects (References required)
•	Experience in designing and developing data migration solutions for
product, supplier, and material data
•	Expert knowledge of data structures and relational databases
•	Expert knowledge of Excel formulas and Access queries
•	Experience in reporting Data quality using SAP BusinessObjects Data
Quality XI 4.0/3.0/3.1
•	Experience developing data scripts and database development
including triggers and stored procedures
•	Experience with SQL, database, and data manipulation and parsing
tools
•	Should be an independent worker with less supervision

Requirement No3

back end)

packages
```

```
docdwarf@panix.com wrote:
> In article
> <716c79fe-7fa8-453a-8052-b208497cbc20@i2g2000vbv.googlegroups.com>,
…[16 more quoted lines elided]…
> comp.lang.cobol be a target for advertisements by clothiers?

For the same reason it is a target for all the other nonsense that is off 
topic...

Because they can...

"cloth eared" is a gentle old expression which I have only heard in the UK.

The most memorable instance (for me, anyway...) is in the skit called 
"Interesting Facts" which was written by Peter Cook and performed by him and 
John Cleese at "The Secret Policeman's Ball".

After Cook has been pestering Cleese with a huge mass of inaccurate  "facts" 
Cleese finally explodes and calls him: the most

"...cloth eared, swivel-eyed, fornicating little git..." he has ever met.

Cook eyes him with wonder and says: "Is that a fact?"

I actually queued up to get into this performance at the Haymarket theatre 
in London in 1979. Sadly I missed out as they were full, just as I was only 
a few places away from getting in. Some time later I managed to get the 
video of it and have it to this day.

I thought it would be on youtube and, sure enough...

http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OnxXkjD6VmE

Pete
```

## Thread: Dinosaur Alert - Error Issue — 34 msgs

_Topics: [`COBOL's future, legacy, and obsolescence`](topics.md#future)_

### Dinosaur Alert - Error Issue

- **From:** "Paul Richards" <paulrichards@XXXNOSPAMiinet.net.au>
- **Date:** 2012-03-16T23:12:33-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<Ad6dnfOqn9GskvnSnZ2dnUVZ_umdnZ2d@westnet.com.au>`

```
I have a program which compiles correctly and runs fine using Net
Express.

As the program is a MS-DOS/Screen Section/ADIS app I tried to compile
it for MS-DOS in MicroFocus 3.1.54 but receive a Fatal error.

I'm creating a dynamic table and populating it with records read from a
file:

*--- dynamic table                                      
 linkage section.                                       
 01 dataList occurs 1 to 250 depending on artist-cnt    
             ascending key is tblArtistRef              
             indexed by tbl-index.                      
    03 tblartist-rec.                                   
       05 tblArtistRef          pic x(6).               
       05 tblArtistTitle        pic x(35). 
..........             
             
The error occurs when the compiler parses the populating code: 
                                           
populate-memory-table.         *> read file and add records to   
 move eof-false to eof-status  *> memory table                   
 set tbl-index to 0            *> ERROR HERE <<<<<<

 perform artist-cnt times                                        
   read artist-file next                                         
   set tbl-index up by 1                                         
   move  artist-rec to tblartist-rec(tbl-index)                  
 end-perform                                                     
 set tbl-index to 1.           *> reset index for display start  


Error display:

"set tbl-index to 0
 ------------------
 Wrong combination of data types

 MFHXX Error 166
 Recursive Cobol Call is illegal"

Any ideas why my old COBOL compiler produces these errors and the
'modern' one doesn't? Can I recode this to avoid the error?

This is a personal hobby/interest project so I'd appreciate not
receiving admonishments for 'living in the past' etc :-)

TIA
```

#### ↳ Re: Dinosaur Alert - Error Issue

- **From:** Rick Smith <rs847925@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2012-03-16T22:56:33-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<10973219.2055.1331963793982.JavaMail.geo-discussion-forums@yncd8>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<Ad6dnfOqn9GskvnSnZ2dnUVZ_umdnZ2d@westnet.com.au>`
- **References:** `<Ad6dnfOqn9GskvnSnZ2dnUVZ_umdnZ2d@westnet.com.au>`

```
On Saturday, March 17, 2012 12:12:33 AM UTC-4, Paul Richards wrote:
> I have a program which compiles correctly and runs fine using Net
> Express.
…[41 more quoted lines elided]…
> 'modern' one doesn't? Can I recode this to avoid the error?

'SET index-name TO 0' is invalid in COBOL 85. however
COBOL 02 was changed to allow the statement. I suggest
the combination

    set tbl-index to 1
    set tbl-index down by 1

You have not supplied any code for recursion. If
recursion is intended, add a LOCAL-STORAGE SECTION
in WORKING-STORAGE. If recursion was not intended,
correct the SET statement and see what happens.


> This is a personal hobby/interest project so I'd appreciate not
> receiving admonishments for 'living in the past' etc :-)
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> Melbourne,  Australia
```

```
* Data:         516     Code:          68
=====

Without flagging I get the same error.

> > however
> > COBOL 02 was changed to allow the statement.

=====
ISO/IEC 1989:2002(E)
Substantive changes not affecting existing programs

121) SET index-name. The result of setting an index can be
outside of the range of the associated table. Also, the
setting of an index in the TO phrase does not have to be
within the range of the associated table.
=====

Note the specific reference to the "TO phrase", which
implies that COBOL 85 had stricter requirements;
i.e., 0 was not permitted since it could never be
within the range of a table.
```

```
Rick Smith wrote:
> On Saturday, March 17, 2012 3:37:27 PM UTC-4, Richard wrote:
>> On Mar 17, 6:56 pm, Rick Smith <rs847...@gmail.com> wrote:
…[15 more quoted lines elided]…
> within the range of a table.

COBOL is the ONLY language I know of where zero is NOT in the range of a 
table.

So, COBOL '85 doesn't allow it (which gels with my own experience) and COBOL 
2002 allows it, but that standard has little credibility and has never been 
fully implemented.

Conclusion: Best avoided. Don't set indexes or subscripts to zero if they 
are referencing anything. (I have sometimes set an index to 1, then set it 
down by 1 in an initialization routine, before it is used. (The loop code 
would increment it before using it)  But mostly I let PERFORM control them 
and they start at 1...)

Pete.
```

```
On Thu, 22 Mar 2012 14:02:07 +1300, "Pete Dashwood"
<dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:

>Richard wrote:
>> On Mar 21, 6:11 pm, "Pete Dashwood"
…[27 more quoted lines elided]…
>Not that I care, you understand :-)...


Basic originally certainly did not.  MS implementations have long
supported "OPTION BASE".  IIRC, all IBM PC versions defaulted to 0,
but (at least some) other earlier MS implementations defaulted to 1.
And other implementations never had the option, and were always 1
(Applesoft Basic on the Apple II  - which is MS - was always 1, for
example).  HP-2000 Basic was always 1.  The original Dartmouth Basic
was not.

And I think you may be misremembering about F77.  Arrays were
definitely (only) base 1 in older standards (FIV, for example).  In
(at least) F90 and later you could specify array ranges Pascal style
(IOW, "REAL, DIMENSION(-5:14)"), but I'm 98% certain that was *not* in
F77.  In any event, the default is still base 1 (IOW, if you
"DIMENSION B(100)", accessing B(0) *is* an error).

Obviously particular implementations may have had various extensions.

But the debate between base 0 and base 1 arrays is ancient, and was
often a distinction between "application" and "system" languages.  And
is the basis of one of my favorite CS quotes:

"Should array indices start at 0 or 1? My compromise of 0.5 was
rejected without, I thought, proper consideration." - Stan
Kelly-Bootle
```

```
That is true of Fortran 77, a different language, but FORTRAN in the
previous two decades had the first array item as 1.

> I tend to be unconventional... :-)
>
> Algol, I don't know about and will take your word

I can photocopy a page of the manual if required.

> I understood Pascal could define array bounds (as you noted). I believe that
> definition can include zero, much as for Fortran.

You mean 'much as in Fortran _77_'.

ISO Pascal does allow any subscript range, including negative, but
that is a different language from 'Pascal' as created by Wirth.

> It is a long time since I wrote BASIC but Microsoft Basic (and Visual Basic)
> certainly allow array(0).

'BASIC' is not one language but is a class of, often quite different,
languages that have vague similarities. Which is why I said 'some'.

Some versions of MS BASIC and DRI Personal BASIC have an 'OPTION BASE'
statement which can set the minimum subscript to 0 or 1 as required.

JEAN is another language with subscripts starting at 1. This was an
interactive language for ICL 1900 series and GEORGE* III from the
1960s (or possibly, like the other George III, from the 1760s). Yes, I
still have a manual for that too, alongside my PLAN and PERT manuals.



* General ORGanizational Environment.

> Not that I care, you understand :-)...

> Pete.
> --
> "I used to write COBOL...now I can do anything."
```

```
If it were me, I would try deleting the line that sets tbl-index to zero 
and then recoding the loop as follows:

  perform varying tbl-index from 1 by 1
          until   tbl-index > artist-cnt
    read artist-file next
    set tbl-index up by 1
    move  artist-rec to tblartist-rec(tbl-index)
  end-perform
  set tbl-index to 1.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Dinosaur Alert - Error Issue

- **From:** Richard <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>

```
"Paul Richards" <paulrichards@XXXNOSPAMiinet.net.au> wrote in

I have no experience with this particular compiler, but it looks to me as though it wants the 
value of an index to be a positive integer.
> 
>  perform artist-cnt times                                        
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
>  set tbl-index to 1.           *> reset index for display start  

Try this instead:

populate-memory-table.         
 move eof-false to eof-status 
 set tbl-index to 1    	    	*> Note set to 1 instead of 0
 
 perform artist-cnt times                                        
   read artist-file next                                         
   move  artist-rec to tblartist-rec(tbl-index)   *> Note order of these two
   set tbl-index up by 1                                         *> statements is reversed
 end-perform                                                     
 set tbl-index to 1.
```

#### ↳ Re: Dinosaur Alert - Error Issue

- **From:** Richard <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-03-17T12:12:16-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9f690386-3f6f-42eb-b359-10927d1c102d@gj7g2000pbc.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<Ad6dnfOqn9GskvnSnZ2dnUVZ_umdnZ2d@westnet.com.au>`

```
On Mar 17, 5:12 pm, "Paul Richards"
<paulricha...@XXXNOSPAMiinet.net.au> wrote:
> I have a program which compiles correctly and runs fine using Net
> Express.
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> file:

No, you are not creating a dynamic table, at least not in MF 3.x.

An OCCURS 1 TO 250 will create a fixed memory array of 250 items. The
'depending on' will be used to set a limit for some operations such as
SEARCH and MOVE.

> *--- dynamic table
>  linkage section.
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> ..........

In LINKAGE SECTION no memory area will be created (in MF 3.1) by the
compiler. It is usual that another program will have an area in their
working-storage and will pass it to this program as a parameter to a
CALL. There may be other means of creating a memory area that this
will map to, such as using a system call to create a memory area then
using SET to point dataList at that. This is not valid '85 COBOL but
is a MF extension in this compiler.

An OCCURS on an 01 level is wrong. An 01 is a record area, OCCURS can
only be on a group or elementary item. Some compilers will process
this as if it were a group, others may not.

Both to comply and logically the OCCURS should be on tblArtist-rec.

That is to say you are not creating 250 '01 records', but are creating
one '01 array record' that contains 250 items.


> The error occurs when the compiler parses the populating code:
>
…[17 more quoted lines elided]…
>  Recursive Cobol Call is illegal"

Because it is in LINKAGE SECTION then it won't exist unless:

a) it has been passed as a CALL parameter from a program where it does
exist, and this is specified on the PROCEDURE DIVISION header.

or b) some other means has been used to create it, such as a system
call to create the memory area.

It is likely that tbl-index does not exist and thus the compiler
cannot determine what it is.

> Any ideas why my old COBOL compiler produces these errors and the
> 'modern' one doesn't? Can I recode this to avoid the error?

Newer compilers have more features. It may be that MF 3.1 DOS compiler
does not automatically create tbl-index because it is in LINKAGE but
later compilers 'fixed' this issue.


> This is a personal hobby/interest project so I'd appreciate not
> receiving admonishments for 'living in the past' etc :-)
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Dinosaur Alert - Error Issue

- **From:** Richard <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-03-19T22:12:21-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<d638157a-c5cf-4d69-a669-be946595617f@o3g2000pbt.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<Ad6dnfOqn9GskvnSnZ2dnUVZ_umdnZ2d@westnet.com.au> <XqqdnR3e68CBo_jSnZ2dnUVZ_rqdnZ2d@westnet.com.au>`

```
On Mar 18, 2:45 pm, "Paul Richards"
<paulricha...@XXXNOSPAMiinet.net.au> wrote:
> Gentlemen: thanks for your helpful comments.

> With respect to the general design and Richard's final comments, I used
> this example to base my approach on
>
> http://itsacobolworld.blogspot.com.au/2010/06/declarative-sorting-of-dyn
> amically.html (although I'm not sorting the table contents)

I looked at that example and have these comments:

       01 variants occurs 1 to 1000 depending on variant-count
                   ascending key is sku
                   indexed   by jump-start-index.
           03 sku  binary-long.
           03 decr pic x(20).

In ANS'85 OCCURS is not allowed on 01 or 77 level. MF allow this as
[confusing] non-standard item.

In particular an 01 is a record area so one may expect it to unroll
as:

      01  variants(1).
          03 sku(1) ..
          03 decr(1) ...
      01  variants(2).
          03 sku(2) ..
          03 decr(2) ...
      01  ...

But there may be padding between 01 level items. Adding a 02 to take
the occurs makes it standard and more clear (IMHO).

       01 variants.
           02 SKU-Items occurs 1 to 1000 depending on variant-count
                   ascending key is sku
                   indexed   by jump-start-index.
             03 sku  binary-long.
             03 decr pic x(20).

Here is where confusion could occur:

           move 10 to variant-count
           set mem-ln to length of variants

Setting variant-count to 10 gives 10 sku and decr. Is the 'length of'
the data area of 'variants' refer to the total size of the table or of
one occurs ?  In fact in the original it does give 24, but I would
change this to:

           set mem-ln to length of SKU-Items(1)

to make this explicit. We see inconsistencies appear in:

           set address of variants(1) to mem-ptr

which is clearer as:

           set address of variants   to mem-ptr

The SORT also needs changing to SORT SKU-Items.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Dinosaur Alert - Error Issue

- **From:** Richard <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-03-19T23:20:36-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9f7136c9-39ea-45c8-94f0-67761aec7458@oq7g2000pbb.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<Ad6dnfOqn9GskvnSnZ2dnUVZ_umdnZ2d@westnet.com.au> <XqqdnR3e68CBo_jSnZ2dnUVZ_rqdnZ2d@westnet.com.au>`

```
On Mar 18, 2:45 pm, "Paul Richards"
<paulricha...@XXXNOSPAMiinet.net.au> wrote:
> Gentlemen: thanks for your helpful comments.
>
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> in Net Express.

In MF 3.1 the default is that memory is initialized to spaces. The
SPZERO compiler option will cater for display numeric items containing
spaces to be treated as zero, _BUT_ this only works for 'native' code.
ie .gnt or .exe, compiled with OPT(1) or OPT(2). As this OPT() only
applies in the generate phase then it won't be used when running the
program from the editor or animator, or when the compiler output is
a .int or equivalent.

The Net Express version may well apply SPZERO, or some equivalent, all
the time.

You may be using a numeric data item when it has non-numeric
characters. This may be because you are, for example, ADDing to a W-S
item that does not have a VALUE clause nor has it been initialized.

Or you are reading a data item from a file that has non-numeric
characters in a numeric field. eg "   123456" instead of "000123456"
when the field is PIC S9(7)V99.

Ensure that W-S numeric fields have a VALUE clause or MOVE ZERO to
them before using them.

For all input use a IF NUMERIC test. It is necessary to do this on a
PIC X() redefines or group field - you can't do IF NUMERIC on a
NUMERIC field in ANS'85.

> With respect to the general design and Richard's final comments, I used
> this example to base my approach on
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
> releasing any memory.

You are creating the table 'dynamically' in that you are creating it
at run-time rather than compile time, but it is not a 'dynamic table'
because it will not change the physical size by changing the value of
the depending on.  If you wanted it larger than the original size it
was created at you would have to CBL_FREE_MEM and then CBL_ALLOC_MEM
with a larger size, and that would lose all the data in it.
```

#### ↳ Re: Dinosaur Alert - Error Issue - SOLVED

- **From:** "Paul Richards" <paulrichards@XXXNOSPAMiinet.net.au>
- **Date:** 2012-03-19T20:04:31-05:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<HOydnYR8UOYCSvrSnZ2dnUVZ_qidnZ2d@westnet.com.au>`
- **References:** `<Ad6dnfOqn9GskvnSnZ2dnUVZ_umdnZ2d@westnet.com.au>`

```
Paul Richards wrote:

> I have a program which compiles correctly and runs fine using Net
> Express.
…[46 more quoted lines elided]…
> TIA

I think the cause of this problem had nothing to do with the apparent
symptom. As is so often the case, the solution was straightforward. My
data and index files are in a WORK folder. I realised that the
Professional COBOL editor was defaulting to the MFCOBOL\EXEDLL folder.
Since I was running the prgram from within the editor, I guess that
when I was using the function that required the dynamic memory
allocation and reading of data from a file the program could not find
the file (since it must have been 'looking' in EXEDLL) and this sparked
off a series of strange conditions which the compiler attempted to
analyse and provide messages for. My analysis may, of course, be
totally off the mark but the solution below has solved the issue.

The solution was,in my batch file which sets up the PROCO environment,
to issue a final 'change directory' command to the WORK folder. After
this the program works as it should and there is, therefore, no
apparent conflict with the Net Express compilation.

It also means that 'set tbl-index to 0' is a valid statement in version
3.1.54 since I reverted to my original coding and produced the expected
results.

Thanks once again for the advice received earlier.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Dinosaur Alert - Error Issue - SOLVED

- **From:** Rick Smith <rs847925@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2012-03-20T16:09:00-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<13711866.327.1332284940959.JavaMail.geo-discussion-forums@yneo2>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<HOydnYR8UOYCSvrSnZ2dnUVZ_qidnZ2d@westnet.com.au>`
- **References:** `<Ad6dnfOqn9GskvnSnZ2dnUVZ_umdnZ2d@westnet.com.au> <HOydnYR8UOYCSvrSnZ2dnUVZ_qidnZ2d@westnet.com.au>`

```
On Monday, March 19, 2012 9:04:31 PM UTC-4, Paul Richards wrote:
[snip]

> It also means that 'set tbl-index to 0' is a valid statement in version
> 3.1.54 since I reverted to my original coding and produced the expected
> results.

That is an invalid conclusion! As I demonstrated
elsewhere, Micro Focus 3.2 (with COBOL 85 flagging)
does flag such a statement as an error. In reaching
your conclusion, you failed to account for the
possibility that Micro Focus 3.1 was not in
conformance with standard COBOL for that variant
of the SET statement. 

IOW 'set tbl-index to 0' is invalid in COBOL 85
and the failure of any implementation (claiming
conformance to COBOL 85) to flag the statement
cannot make the statement valid.
```

<a id="t-1e3d6b0f28"></a>
## Thread: COBOL on tap — 6 msgs

### COBOL on tap

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-03-18T03:10:17+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9sjkabFlcmU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
There are a number of reasons why people may be currently seeking to limit 
their further investment in COBOL.

I find myself needing COBOL compilation ability to provide components and 
executables for generated source code, but I stopped paying for COBOL 
maintenance and support some years back, and do not intend to invest further 
into it.

Many people just go with what their vendor tells them and keep upgrading 
even though the upgrades seldom deliver anything exciting or new, and they 
keep support paid up because it means a cheaper upgrade, even though the 
"support" (if they even need it) can leave much to be desired.

Mainly for my own convenience I developed scripts that allow me to run COBOL 
on ONE machine  but have any number of machines access it on the LAN. The 
vendor says this is not possible but it seems to work OK... My applications 
(if they need a COBOL compiler) can run one locally or remotely. I have been 
looking at legal ways to distribute a compiler with my application software 
but it is too hard and too expensive for the clients and for me.

The Cloud looks like an obvious solution.

ONE copy of a licensed compiler runnning on ONE core in the cloud with 
access on demand when compiles are needed.  COBOL on tap... it is just a 
logical extension of what I'm currently doing on the LAN. It is a bit like 
having a chair in front of a computer that runs COBOL. Different people can 
sit in the chair without violating the ONE Seat/ONE Machine licence.

You may remember that a little while back Gary Crook posted here announcing 
elastic COBOL. COBOL runnning in the Cloud.

I've taken another look at this service and I think it is excellent. The 
elastic compiler generates Java, which is not useful to me as a Microsoft 
developer, but I'm sure many people would find this handy. The concept is 
imaginative and simple. From a user point of view, you always have the 
latest version of COBOL, no upgrades required, can access your development 
machine from any location, and have all the housekeeping done for you 
(backups, hardware expansion, etc.) And you only pay when you use it.

I had a chat with my hosting ISP (who is amazing), to see if he has any 
plans for Cloud support. He hasn't currently but he gave me some excellent 
advice about setting up a private cloud and exposing a machine on my own 
premises, so clients can access it. I've had enough practice now at writing 
Web Services to be able to provide the necessary one very quickly, and I'll 
use a VM running on a dedicated server. The point about VMs is that you can 
snapshot them and restore them if problems arise... You can be fixing what 
went wrong, without the service coming down.

With Public Cloud availability getting over 98%, the old chestnut about not 
having COBOL available without Internet access sounds a bit thin. I'll start 
off with a Private Cloud so I can test the water, but once it is all ticking 
over I could make it Public.

I'll more than likely go ahead with this as soon as I have the time, but I'd 
be interested to hear what anyone thinks in terms of pros and cons.

Would you consider COBOL on tap for your own purposes?

Do you really need the trouble and expense of an on site COBOL compiler in 
2012? Why continue paying for upgrades and support that are really 
neither...?

If you can run one-off and batch compilation remotely, for a fraction of the 
cost of doing it on-site, why wouldn't you?

I believe Elastic COBOL is defintiely a step in the right direction.

Pete.
```

#### ↳ Re: COBOL on tap

- **From:** Richard <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-03-17T12:52:00-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<f4ceccc7-6545-429b-9b1d-d10c99c0374d@to5g2000pbc.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<9sjkabFlcmU1@mid.individual.net>`

```
On Mar 18, 3:10 am, "Pete Dashwood"
<dashw...@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
> There are a number of reasons why people may be currently seeking to limit
> their further investment in COBOL.
…[13 more quoted lines elided]…
> vendor says this is not possible but it seems to work OK...

You should carefully read your licence agreement, and then reread it
pretending that you are your vendor's legal team (you may get a
completely different result I have found).

Compilers may be licenced on a 'per developer' basis and not a 'per
install'. In particular I had been told by Fujitsu that installing on
a server for shared access, rather than on each developer's desktop,
was not allowed, even though the licence did not explicitly state
this.

It probably won't matter for your own internal use but putting it on
the internet would be asking for trouble.

> My applications
> (if they need a COBOL compiler) can run one locally or remotely. I have been
…[52 more quoted lines elided]…
> "I used to write COBOL...now I can do anything."
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: COBOL on tap

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-03-18T12:21:34+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9skkk0FdtnU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<9sjkabFlcmU1@mid.individual.net> <f4ceccc7-6545-429b-9b1d-d10c99c0374d@to5g2000pbc.googlegroups.com>`

```
Richard wrote:
> On Mar 18, 3:10 am, "Pete Dashwood"
> <dashw...@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote:
…[21 more quoted lines elided]…
> completely different result I have found).

That is sound advice and I already did that. I went further and had it 
reviewed by an expert in these areas.

Basically, if something is not written into a contract (a Licence qualifies 
as a contract) and the spirit of the agreement is not being broken, then the 
agreement, as written, must be adhered to. The Licence is per SEAT; there is 
nothing that says different people can't sit in that seat. If you buy a 5 
seat licence there is no reason why 20 people can't use those 5 seats. The 
Licence doesn't have an individual name on it and no one would buy it if it 
did. Suppose you have to replace an employee who leaves?

Understand that this would be an obsolete and unsupported version of the 
compiler and not the latest offering (which is of no use to me anyway.)
I'll support it myself  as I have been for some years now...

It is not competing with the vendor's current range or diminishing their 
current business. You can't buy this product from them.


>
> Compilers may be licenced on a 'per developer' basis and not a 'per
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> this.

How can they expect people to read their minds? If it isn't in the agreement 
then it isn't true.

I was told it was not technically possible. It is, and I did it.  If the 
license is per machine and not per developer then it is fine for different 
people to use the same machine. If the license is per developer, then as a 
developer I should be able to install it on as many of my machines as I 
want. But I can't. (Unless I buy a multi-seat licence.) They can't have it 
both ways and no Court in the world is going to let them.

You can bet that the terms of the Licence will be changed any time now. :-)

 However, the copy I am using stands on the copy of the Licence I have.



>
> It probably won't matter for your own internal use but putting it on
> the internet would be asking for trouble.

Yes, you're probably right. Maybe I'll just wait until someone else does 
it... :-)

A Private Cloud is just an extended LAN. I have no intention of providing 
public access. The only reason I would move to a Public Cloud would be 
because I didn't want the hassle of maintaining the server, not so that 
every man and his dog could access COBOL. In other words, access would be 
strictly regulated.

Besides, it is an interesting challenge and I'd like to have a crack at it 
:-).

Thanks for your thoughts, Richard.

Pete
```

```
 From my point of view there is no shortage of available COBOL

COBOL jobs at high wages they want to receive.

The article seems to imply that some shops will be forced to abandon 
COBOL and convert applications to something else (Java?  C#?) due to a
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Interesting article

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2012-03-20T23:47:57+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9sr5j0FbpU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<N5adnarR0OXzK_rSnZ2dnUVZ_rCdnZ2d@westnet.com.au> <jk8g71$fot$2@reader1.panix.com> <bbOdncb3OZi5uvXSnZ2dnUVZ5t2dnZ2d@giganews.com>`

```
Arnold Trembley wrote:
> On 3/19/2012 6:41 PM, docdwarf@panix.com wrote:
>> In article<N5adnarR0OXzK_rSnZ2dnUVZ_rCdnZ2d@westnet.com.au>,
…[24 more quoted lines elided]…
> course I could be wrong.  Pete will probably want to disagree.  :-)

On the contrary Arnold, I too found the article's position that certain 
shops may be forced to abandon COBOL because of a lack of programmers, to be 
ludicrous. It simply reinforces my belief that some of the IT management 
around just doesn't get it.

They will be forced to abandon COBOL because the time for COBOL is nearly 
over, the paradigm has changed, and because they didn't have the brains or 
balls to plan for it years ago when it would have been much less traumatic.

I already responded in this thread with my thoughts about this and, by a 
strange coincidence, I have been commisioned to write an article on the 
subject for a very lively developer website (mainly populated by Java guys).

Some of the phrases in my responses here will probably find their way into 
the finished article. :-)

When you are being paid to write something (no matter how reasonable the 
sponsor may be) it is always at the back of your mind that you don't want to 
be too hard on them... :-) I will say what I believe (I always do...)  but 
I'll try to keep it fair and reasonable. (Instead of my usual unfair and 
unreasonable as I can do here with impunity :-))

The important thing here is not about what language you move to (some people 
simply buy a package), it is about ensuring that FUNCTIONALITY  (and that 
includes functionality buried deep in legacy COBOL systems) is made 
available to the business. Modern languages encapsulate functionality (with 
reusable Classes and object instances of those Classes) better than COBOL 
does; that is really the main reason for its decline. Modern COBOL can do it 
too, but it is harder to write and most COBOL people take time to make the 
necessary mental adjustments. The ones that do move to OO COBOL use it for a 
while, then realise the other languages are much easier to write and can do 
more, so they just move on.

It was interesting to see the comments in the article about why people 
stopped using COBOL.

Give it three years... :-) (2015...)

Pete.
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Interesting article

- **From:** billg999@cs.uofs.edu (Bill Gunshannon)
- **Date:** 2012-03-22T21:55:05+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9t1ldpF7oqU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<N5adnarR0OXzK_rSnZ2dnUVZ_rCdnZ2d@westnet.com.au> <jk8g71$fot$2@reader1.panix.com>`

```
In article <jk8g71$fot$2@reader1.panix.com>,
	docdwarf@panix.com () writes:
> In article <N5adnarR0OXzK_rSnZ2dnUVZ_rCdnZ2d@westnet.com.au>,
> Paul Richards <paulrichards@XXXNOSPAMiinet.net.au> wrote:
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> increased cost.

Some of you may recall my past lament about an inability to find a COBOL
job that wasn't more interested in CICS andf JCL than in COBOL.

Well, I finally did it.  I am  now working on MicroFocus COBOL on AIX
with an Oracle database.  

I am sure it will please Pete to no end that they are talking of converting
all of this to PL/Sql and Crystal Reports.  Of course, as I have said in the
past, the justification for this has  nothing to do with any real or even
perceived shortcoming in COBOL.  The primary driving factor is the inability
to find COBOL programmers.  

The good news for mew is that there is more than enough COBOL work to take
me up to my real retirement.  The bad news is the level of work required
is primarily because this is by far the worst COBOL I have ever seen.  I
have seen better COBOL turned out by undergrads with little more than a
months worth of COBOL classroom and coding experience.  It started on an
IBM 4381 and has had at least one system migration and three database
migrations.  In every case nothing was done beyond the minimal patching
that was needed to get the programs to run,  There were no programming
standards and no mangerial supervision so every programmer added his/her
own little nuances to the programs.  There are more GO TO's than in a 
BASIC program.  :-)

As for the work these program do.  There is no language available that
would offer any advantage to accomplishing their tasks.

So, if people realy think COBOL is dying, the above would explain why, and
not some notion that COBOL is somehow inadequate.

bill
```

```
Bill Gunshannon wrote:
> In article <jk8g71$fot$2@reader1.panix.com>,
> docdwarf@panix.com () writes:
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
> COBOL job that wasn't more interested in CICS andf JCL than in COBOL.

Yes, I remember it well... :-)

>
> Well, I finally did it.  I am  now working on MicroFocus COBOL on AIX
> with an Oracle database.

Congratulations, Bill. I'm glad this happened for you.
>
> I am sure it will please Pete to no end that they are talking of
> converting all of this to PL/Sql and Crystal Reports.

I think that many people have misunderstood my posts.

First off, I don't care what some installation, far away from me and which I 
am never likely to come in contact with, is doing.

Secondly, I have no vested interest in people moving away from COBOL (unless 
they decide to use the PRIMA toolset to help them do so :-))

So, I am neither pleased nor saddened by their decision.

I AM pleased you have a job and it is a job you have been looking for for 
some time.

> Of course, as
> I have said in the past, the justification for this has  nothing to
> do with any real or even perceived shortcoming in COBOL.

I am on record as saying, in numerous places, most recently, here: 
http://primacomputing.co.nz/cobol21/COBOLRelevance.aspx , that the decline 
in COBOL has nothing to do with flaws or shortcomings in the language. COBOL 
has done what it was designed to do.

> The primary
> driving factor is the inability to find COBOL programmers.
>
I see that as a management shortcoming and, again, I'm on record as saying 
so publicly. Please see my response to the OP in this very thread, posted 
just a few days ago. I have also written a commissioned article for a 
Developer web site where I explore this a bit more. It should be published 
in the next week or so and I'll post a link when it is.

People are looking for alternatives to COBOL and the shortage of programmers 
is only one of the factors why they are doing it.  The bottom line is that 
networked systems need OO and  there are other tools that fit the OO 
paradigm better than COBOL does. Mostly they are free and COBOL isn't, but, 
much more importantly, they achieve more in less time and that means less 
cost. It isn't the fault of COBOL. The world has simply moved on and 
computing has become distributed in a way which nobody could have envisioned 
in 1959 when COBOL was invented.

> The good news for mew is that there is more than enough COBOL work to
> take me up to my real retirement.  The bad news is the level of work
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> programmer added his/her own little nuances to the programs.

Welcome to the real world! :-)

I spent around 20 years encountering this kind of nonsense on sites all 
around the world. After a while you get blase about it. I remember 
complaining bitterly to a manager in Germany  about the horriffic code on 
the site and the fact that it was almost impossible to maintain. He heard me 
out then said simply: "Pete, it's only COBOL..." He was right and I never 
forgot it.

Call yourself a COBOL Programmer? Don't bleat about it, fix it. :-) (Not 
aimed at you personally, Bill, just a general observation...)

> There
> are more GO TO's than in a
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> would offer any advantage to accomplishing their tasks.

And you can say that because you are proficient in every computer 
programming language ever devised, right? :-)

The funny thing about programming is that it ISN'T about languages. A good 
programmer can create solutions in ANY language, provided that language 
implements Djikstra's three operations. (Sequence, Selection, Iteration). 
THAT's when you start to realise that some languages are better suited to 
certain tasks than others are, and you stop being a "One Trick Pony". (As 
Doc has remarked here on occasion: "A good programmer can write Fortran in 
any language"...) Even OO programming requires use of these procedural 
elements on occasion, within Methods, for example...

I have never suggested that you CAN'T do network stuff in COBOL; only that 
Java and C# are better suited for it.

The new generation of programmers, even though they may lack COBOL skills, 
are better trained than most of us were and they understand "programming" 
better than we did. What took many of us years of experience to realise is 
handed to todays programmers in their University courses.

I have worked with a few of them and they can pick up COBOL very quickly. 
The argument that there are no COBOL programmers around is simply nonsense. 
It is presented by short sighted managers who failed to prepare for the 
advent of distributed and networked systems into their organizations. The 
same kind of people who insist that if you haven't got "CICS" on your 
resume, you are useless to them; people who don't understand what is 
involved and recruit based on keywords and buzzwords that they have never 
used themselves and have no understanding of. If you have CICS on a site and 
you need people, of course you will prefer people with CICS experience, but 
if they are thin on the ground, you would take someone with some years of 
COBOL (especially if they have worked on TP apps with another TP monitor) 
and you would know they will be productive within a few weeks.

For myself, (and I have actually done this...) if I can't get COBOL people 
I'll take people with the right attitude and some programming and train 
them. Typically it is weeks rather than months before they are doing useful 
work. If you don't take anybody, you can wait for months and then sob to 
your senior management team that there are "no COBOL programmers available".

>
> So, if people realy think COBOL is dying, the above would explain
> why, and not some notion that COBOL is somehow inadequate.

I shall now reveal to you an amazing secret:  Poor, even dreadful, code 
exists in EVERY language. The quality of code that is written has nothing to 
do with the adequacy of a given programming language.

Pete.
```

```
On 3/22/2012 8:33 PM, Pete Dashwood wrote:
> Bill Gunshannon wrote:
>> In article<jk8g71$fot$2@reader1.panix.com>,
…[144 more quoted lines elided]…
> Pete.

Excellent points Pete (as expected, I might add: happy belated birthday 
as well...)

It is not surprising to find complete spaghetti code in any systems that 
have been around for decades. I would point out something that a lot of 
programmers tend to forget: if you undertake to 'clean up' a program 
that contains a lot of spaghetti code, you take on a huge task of 
testing the resulting program.

It is quite a serious risk to clean up a program that is a mess when 
that program is in production! Most sites I have visited in the last 40 
years do not have a decent testing methodology and certainly would be 
very ill-equipped to provide anything like test suites with verification 
data etc.

It is one thing to put a localized change in a program and convince 
yourself that 'it should work' but quite another to have the confidence 
to say the same if almost the entire program was "restructured".

Actually, in either case (a "trivial and localized change" and a 
complete rewrite) the program *should* be thoroughly tested against a 
set of canned scenarios with careful attention to file comparisons 
before and after etc.

Of course, the problem I am describing is independent of the programming 
language or system being used, but COBOL often gets the blame just 
because...
```

```
Kerry Liles" <"kerry.liles[minus_the_spam] wrote:
> On 3/22/2012 8:33 PM, Pete Dashwood wrote:
>> Bill Gunshannon wrote:
…[151 more quoted lines elided]…
> birthday as well...)

Thanks, Kerry :-)
>
> It is not surprising to find complete spaghetti code in any systems
…[22 more quoted lines elided]…
> blame just because...

I thought about my own experiences after reading the above and I agree it is 
very true that COBOL gets blamed for what is often just bad practice. I can 
think of a couple of occasions when people had a hard time in code review 
and blamed the language... (It was COBOL).

Personally, I've always enjoyed writing COBOL and was doing it again today 
:-)

OK, I don't like the IDE (it is Fujitsu NetCOBOL) and it takes a fair bit of 
code but there is a simple elegance about it that is very satisfying. I 
realized today that I miss the things like bookmarks, regions, (where you 
can make blocks of code disappear so they don't clutter your screen but 
recall them with a mouse click), Intellisense (it is really nice to have the 
IDE show you a prototype signature of the method you just referenced and 
remind you of the type and order of parameters, never mind having it offer 
you valid datanames as you type (bit like pre-emptive texting on a phone, 
which can be a mixed blessing... yet I LOVE it when writing C# in VS)).

I think the thing I groaned about most was having to run up and down code to 
check that datanames are spelled correctly and what their pictures are... 
Intellisense does that for you. I usually end up copying a block of Data 
division code into the procedure division where I'm working so the fields 
are handy for reference, or of course, having another window open with the 
definitions in it, but either way there is a lot of tedious moving about and 
remembering line numbers because you can't bookmark.

The actual coding is the same fun it has always been. :-)

Today I was working on extending a component I wrote nearly 15 years ago. I 
SHOULD have taken the opportunity to rewrite it in C# but I just couldn't do 
it... :-)  There were no changes to the existing interface so regression 
testing shouldn't be necessary. A new method was added, just a couple of 
hundred lines of code and only the applications that need it will use it. 
(It is all because ORACLE sucks so bad :-))

I am becoming more and more persuaded as time goes by that salvaging COBOL 
code is worth the effort. Once it is wrapped it doesn't matter what the 
source language is; it is just an object that provides functionality. And it 
is certainly a lot quicker to refactor COBOL code than to write something 
from scratch, even in a more powerful language with infinitely better tools.

I getting to the point where I think that new functionality will be 
developed in the new languages, but rather than try and replace the existing 
COBOL stuff I'll just mine it and rewrap it.

I'm not paying for COBOL any more (haven't for some years now) and I won't 
be investing further in it. If it turns out something fails and I can't fix 
it (never happened yet), THEN I'll rewrite it in C#... :-)

Pete.
```

- **From:** Arnold Trembley <arnold.trembley@att.net>

- **Message-ID:** `<F5mdnWCCdeo2fPPSnZ2dnUVZ5tmdnZ2d@giganews.com>`

- **References:** `<N5adnarR0OXzK_rSnZ2dnUVZ_rCdnZ2d@westnet.com.au> <jk8g71$fot$2@reader1.panix.com> <9t1ldpF7oqU1@mid.individual.net> <9t1umeFr06U1@mid.individual.net> <9t6si2F9ktU1@mid.individual.net>`
